                <h1 style="clear:both;">Businesses for sale</h1>


<div id="cmsSrpContent" class="cms-sr-content  reducedHeight">

    <div class="cms-text full-width" style="width: 100%">
        
        <div id="cmsSrpContentText" class="cms-text__inner">
            <section class="content">
                <p>Buying a business has many advantages in comparison to starting your own business. It is usually believed to have lesser risks since the initial work has already been done. An established business has procedures and plans in place which can help the new owner navigate the process of running a business.
</p><a id="cmsSrpShowContent" href="javascript:void(0)">Read more</a><br>
<p>There is more certainty as investing in an established business provides cash flow immediately. A financial history allows you to determine what to expect from your business and the loans and investment that you can attract. A crucial advantage of an existing business is that you acquire a network of vendors, staff, equipment, customers, and more. An established market and knowledge from employees are also important advantages.
</p>
<p>Though it can be a bit more costly to buy instead of starting your own business, you would find it easier to obtain financing. This is because banks are aware that your business made profits in the past and are therefore more willing to help you invest in it. When you purchase a business, you may get legal rights pertaining to trademarks, copyright, and more which can protect your work.&nbsp;
</p>
<p>BizQuest is one of the leading platforms where you can find information on buying a business for sale, selling a business, and investing in a franchise. You can perform your research on thousands of businesses that are on sale and connect with them with any inquiries.&nbsp;
</p>
<h2>Figuring Out What Type of Business You Want to Buy</h2>
<p>Once you have made the decision to buy a business, think about what kind of business you want to invest in. The first step involves compiling a list of your interests, passions, and experiences. If you are interested in or familiar with a certain type of industry, you will feel more motivated to own a business within the same industry.
</p>
<p>In addition to interest, you need to have sufficient knowledge of an industry. You can attain this through research on your chosen industry. Following identification of a business and industry type, think about the size of the business you want. This includes the number of locations and employees it currently has. Gather sales information pertaining to businesses within your industry and think about what sales figure you are interested in.
</p>
<p>Finding the right type of business also involves locating the geographical area where you wish to have your own business. Consider fixed costs such as rent, salaries, etc., and variable costs such as raw materials that apply to your business in the same area. Ensure that these costs are compatible with your financial abilities. Think about your future goals for the business and consider whether the area provides opportunities for expansion.
</p>
<p>When you have chosen the ideal geographic area, conduct a search on the list of available businesses which cater to your needs. You can perform your search on BizQuest. You can get access to listings of businesses that are on sale nationwide. Select a business that interests you and learn more about it, such as its history, cashflow, revenue, and more.
</p>
<p><span>You could also connect with a business broker who is typically hired by the selling entity to find a buyer and negotiate the selling price. Brokers are paid a commission, but their assistance is useful for many first-time buyers. Since they are local to the area, brokers often have good knowledge of established businesses and assist with the negotiation process. They could also help with coordinating all the paperwork, which can reduce any stress that comes with buying a business.</span>
</p>
<h2>Understanding Why a Business is For Sale</h2>
<p>While performing your research on available businesses, make note of the ones that you are interested in. Then, take some time to dig deep and understand why someone is selling their business. A lot of business owners skip this process in an attempt to get the best offers, but very often, rash decisions turn out to be detrimental for new owners.
</p>
<p>There can be many reasons why someone would want to sell their business. They might be opting to retire or move on to another career pursuit. A more negative reason could be a significant flaw in the business itself.&nbsp;
</p>
<p><span>Try to speak with the current owner and learn why they are interested in selling their business. Consider asking what challenges they faced with their business, what steps were implemented to solve the issues, and how the implementation process went. A good investment is where a business shows potential for profit and reduced risk of losing out to competitors. A poor investment is one that is not sustainable, has zero or negative profit margins, and belongs to a highly competitive industry.</span>
</p>
<h2>Due Diligence</h2>
<p>Performing due diligence is a crucial part of understanding whether a business available for purchase is ideal for you. Once you have personally formed an impression about the current business situation from the owner, speak with an advisor such as a lawyer or accountant. They can help verify data and give further advice about the business that you are interested in.
</p>
<p>With assistance from an expert, try to determine answers to the following-
</p>
<ul>
	<li>Reason(s) why the business is for sale</li>
	<li>Is the business earning profits?</li>
	<li>Does it have control over the market share?</li>
	<li>Are supply lines available and functioning well?</li>
	<li>Does the business have a good reputation in the industry and the community?</li>
	<li>Is it possible to expand the business in the future?</li>
</ul>
<p>It is important to understand how well the business is operating from the perspectives of stakeholders. See if you can connect with the existing vendors, clients, and suppliers of the company. Try to learn how the business maintains its professional associations. You can also learn whether the business has any complaints registered against it by contacting a local insurance and business licensing agency.
</p>
<p><span>While gathering pertinent information, be mindful of signs such as large amounts of debt, stiff industry competition, or lack of a well-conceived business plan. Investigate any possible issues with the company brand, location, and stakeholders. Factors such as inventory and equipment should also be examined.</span>
</p>
<h2>Evaluating the Price of a Business</h2>
<p>As part of the evaluation process, consult your attorney and acquisitions personnel to check the financial health and price of your business. Ask your finance team to conduct an analysis of the monetary value of the business. Consider how the owner’s present associations will affect the value.&nbsp;
</p>
<p>There are several ways in which you can measure the fair value during purchasing a business. The capitalized earning method is where the value of a business is assessed by the amount of return that the new owner expects from the investment. The total value of assets is another measure which adds the value of all tangible assets that the business owns and subtracts liabilities from the value. In some cases, you may add expected earnings to this value which would be the revenue you get in addition to net assets.
</p>
<p>The cash flow method, on the other hand, determines how much borrowing the organization’s cash flow can support. You can also use the price-to-earnings (P/E) ratio to assess the income of the company in the coming few years. A positive ratio and earnings in thousands of dollars could indicate a high value for your business. While computing the price of the business, consider other financial issues such as its revenue history and earning abilities, intangible assets, and overall financial health.
</p>
<p>To gain better insights into the company’s financial status and future requirements, obtain copies of projected financial statements. Financial documents are also good indicators of the overall financial situation of a business. Go over the numbers with your accountant and see whether there are any previously undisclosed problems.&nbsp;
</p>
<p>In conclusion, here is a checklist of items you should investigate to assess financial health and fair price of a business-
</p>
<ul>
	<li>Photocopies of contracts and any other legal document</li>
	<li>Financial statements of the previous three to five years</li>
	<li>Inventory</li>
	<li>Physical equipment including furniture, fixtures, and the building</li>
	<li>Tax returns of the last five years</li>
	<li>Liabilities</li>
	<li>Accounts receivable</li>
	<li>Accounts payable</li>
	<li>Sales records</li>
	<li>Insurance</li>
	<li><span>Current employees and entire organizational chart</span></li>
</ul>
<h2>How to buy a business with no money</h2>
<p>Upon selecting your business of choice, determining, and negotiating a fair price, and procuring financing, you are now ready to officially buy the business. Work with your attorney to develop the draft sales agreement which makes the transfer of ownership official. There are a few other documents that you will also need before buying the business.
</p>
<p>In addition to the bill of sale which proves you to be the owner, have a document mentioning the adjusted purchase price which is the final cost of purchase. In case you are leasing the business, ensure that you and the owner agree to the terms of leasing. If the business has vehicles, you will need to transfer their ownership by the time of sale.
</p>
<p>Like business vehicles, all copyrights, patents, and trademarks should be transferred to you by the time of sale. In certain cases, you might need to file franchise documents which you can learn about by checking the Small Business Administration <a href="https://www.sba.gov/offices/headquarters/oee/resources/3641">website</a>. Typically, new business owners choose to have a non-compete business agreement signed by the previous owner. This legal agreement prevents the previous owner from starting a competing business across the street from you.
</p>
<p>If the seller intends to remain in your business as an employee, you will need to draft an employee agreement stating the terms of employment. Make sure that the terms of employment are clear to the seller who will now be an employee. Another statement called the asset acquisition statement is important for filing purposes as it mentions the number of assets you have acquired and their value. This document is crucial for tax returns.
</p>
<p>As a first-time business owner, you need to be aware of the bulk sale laws that are in place within your community. They involve the selling of business inventory and are in place to prohibit business owners from engaging in activities such as selling the business to a different owner and evading moneylenders. You can comply with these laws by informing your local tax authority about the ongoing business sale.
</p>
<p><span>Buying a business offers many opportunities to those interested in exploring entrepreneurship as a career path. By opting to buy an existing business, you avoid uncertainties that come with starting a new business. Not only are businesses necessary for providing essential services to the community, but they are also vital for providing employment opportunities. Investing in a successful business is a great way to step your toes into the entrepreneurial world.</span>
</p>

<script type="text/javascript" defer="">
        $(function () {

            sessionStorage.setItem('bfsLastSearch', 'ltype=40&o=1');
            sessionStorage.setItem('bfsTotalRows', 10000);
            sessionStorage.removeItem('bfsCurrentPosition');

            if (showSavedSearchTout) {
                if (!SavedSearchToutCookieExists()) {
                    var displayed = false;
                    var maxScrollHeight = document.documentElement.scrollHeight - document.documentElement.clientHeight;
                    window.addEventListener("scroll", function(event) {
                        var scrollPercentage = Math.round(window.pageYOffset / maxScrollHeight * 100);
                        if (scrollPercentage > 1 && !displayed) {
                            $('#saveThisSearch1').modal('show');
                            SetSearchCookie();
                            displayed = true;
                            window.removeEventListener('scroll', arguments.callee, false);
                        }
                    });
                    //window.setTimeout(function() {
                    //    $('#saveThisSearch1').modal('show');
                    //    SetSearchCookie();
                    //},3000);
                }

                function SetSearchCookie() {
                    var days = 7;
                    var name = "bqsavedsearchtout";
                    var value = 1;
                    var expireDate = new Date();
                    expireDate.setDate(expireDate.getDate() + days);
                    document.cookie = name + "=" + value + "; path=/; expires=" + expireDate.toGMTString() + ";secure";
                }

                function SavedSearchToutCookieExists() {
                    var bRes = true;
                    try {
                        var Name = "bqsavedsearchtout";
                        var re = new RegExp(Name + "=[^;]*", "i"); /*construct RE to search for target name/value pair */
                        if (document.cookie.match(re)) /*if cookie found*/
                            bRes = true;
                        else
                            bRes = false;
                    } catch (e) {
                    }
                    return bRes;
                }

            }
        });
</script>
